## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and time t (possible external driving). The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and/or periodic driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with quadratic term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic drive)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared drag, sign-preserving)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum with drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Quintic Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potential
- Negative linear coefficient with positive cubic coefficient in x → double-well (bistable) Duffing potential
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v → amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol self-excitation)
- Periodic time dependence cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) → external driving force causing resonance or chaos
- Pure position-dependent acceleration with no v or t terms → conservative (energy-preserving) system
- Linear v term with negative coefficient → energy dissipation (damping); positive coefficient → energy injection
- Products of x and v (e.g., x*v, x²*v) → nonlinear damping that depends on oscillation amplitude
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(c*x) → periodic potential / pendulum-type dynamics with unbounded phase space

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO36)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidate formulas: 67

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT: `F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v`, which is `-0.372947617362308*v*exp(-Abs(x)) + 0.156062620221068*sin(t)`.

The key challenge is the `exp(-Abs(x))` term. Since `Abs(x)` is NOT equivalent to `x` (variables can be negative), I need to check if any candidate can reproduce `exp(-|x|)`.

Note that `exp(-|x|)` equals `exp(-x)` for x≥0 and `exp(x)` for x<0. A single `exp(c*x)` term cannot match this for all x.

Let me check candidates systematically:

**Candidates with just `v*exp(c*x)` as the exponential term (49, 50, etc.):**
These give `c3*v*exp(c4*x)`, which is `v*exp(c4*x)`. Setting c4 to any value gives a monotonic exponential, not `exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x)` + polynomial terms in x (like candidates 1-34, etc.):**
Polynomial corrections to `exp(cx)` cannot make it equal `exp(-|x|)` exactly. **No match.**

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(c*x) + 1)` terms (13, 18, 35, 36):**
Note that `log(exp(ax) + 1)` is related to the softplus function. For `v*log(exp(ax)+1)`, this doesn't directly help create `v*exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates with `sin(c*exp(c*x) + c)` terms (38, 40, 58, 59, 64):**
These create oscillatory functions of exponentials, not `exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates with `exp(c*x^2)` (61):**
`exp(c*x^2)` with c<0 gives a Gaussian, not `exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidates with `v*cos(c*x)` terms (2, 3):**
`cos(cx)` is even in x like `exp(-|x|)`, but `cos(cx)` is periodic while `exp(-|x|)` decays. **No match.**

**Candidate 13: `c7*v*log(c8*exp(c9*x) + 1)`**
Note: `log(exp(-x) + 1) = log(exp(-x)(1 + exp(x))) = -x + log(1 + exp(x))`. And `log(1+exp(x))` is the softplus. For x>0: `log(1+exp(-x)) ≈ exp(-x)` for large x. For x<0: `log(1+exp(x)) ≈ exp(x)` for large |x|. But `log(1+exp(-x))` is NOT exactly `exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 35/36: `c5*log(c6*exp(c7*x) + 1)`** - This isn't multiplied by v, so it can't produce `v*exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidate with `v*x*exp(c*x)` (39, 5, 4, 27):**
`v*exp(cx) + v*x*exp(dx)` - combinations of these still can't produce `exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 64: `exp(c*sin(c*x+c))`** - This is periodic in x. **No match.**

After careful analysis, the fundamental issue is that **none** of the candidates can reproduce `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(-Abs(x))`. Every candidate uses `exp(c*x)` (a monotonic exponential in x), possibly combined with polynomials, trigonometric functions, or logarithms. None of these can exactly equal the non-analytic function `exp(-|x|)` which has a kink at x=0.

The only candidates with `Abs` are candidates 10, 20, 31, 47, 48 — but these have `Abs(v)` or `v*Abs(v)`, not `Abs(x)`. These cannot produce the `exp(-|x|)` term either.

No candidate can match the GT because none can produce `v*exp(-|x|)`.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match
